<Date>1559220884274< /Date><rate>4<//rate><review>Located off Carson in Torrance. Small parking lot shared with other businesses during the day time parking will probably be tight after the other businesses close parking would be better. The place is small they have a big table in the middle to accommodate a big party and a couple of booths along the side and a few rooms to sit Japanese style where you take your shoes off. The staff was friendly and service was pretty fast. I wasn't hungry for ramen so I just got some edamame. Kenny B</username>
<date>1512316895486<//date><Rating>5< /Rating>< Review>
This is your typical Japanese ramen shop: a few tables, a mini bar, and a few booths.

There is a large room on the left upon entering, and is normally occupied. I can say the same towards the booths (towards the right, window view of Carson St) but not as frequent compared to the former.

Service is fantastic, the servers check on you from time to time, unlike other places where they just seat you and, well, good luck getting service!

I get the usual [will update this later of the specific order when I visit again as well as include a picture of the menu(s) for your convenience].

If you're not familiar with Japanese cuisine, the portions are VERY SMALL compared to American cuisine, so don't be surprised if you order anything that ISN'T ramen and find that it looks rather skimpy.

I don't know if they have a customer-usable restroom as I never asked (will add on next visit).

I always come back for the spontaneous ramen cravings!!!<//Review>

Francisco Torres< /Name>
< Text>
Came here because my cousin said it was good so I just had to try it out. Its a fair sized place with i believe 2 enclosed tables, we sat in one of them. It's both a pro and con because yes its enclosed but it made it easy to forget we were there. Also being busy made it easy to forget us since our table wasn't in eye sight. Service could have been a tad better but it was still good. My waitress stayed helpful and positive which is always great. Now as far as food goes I had the takoyaki and small curry rice to start, both of which were great delicious starters. My main course was their spicy miso ramen but I had to add flavored egg and seaweed since I love having both in all my ramen. Be aware that the spicy miso ramen doesn't come with egg already. Almost every other ramen spot I have been to has it already included in the ramen so that was different. The seaweed however wasn't how I prefer seaweed on my ramen. This place had it chopped up and it was moist served on the side. Other spots serve it dried and in 1 or 2 large pieces inside the ramen; that's how I prefer it. Overall the ramen was great and filling. I wish I could try it with sake and dessert but I'll save that for next time. I do recommend this place and I will return for another time.<//Text>

<Rating>5</Rating>< review>
Great place to have that specialty tea. Highly recommend the mangonada smoothie. My first choice for teas is the oolong peach, the earl grey milk teas, and their underrated jasmine milk teas. The owner takes great care providing quality teas. Trust me, she's working in the back making sure your tea is exactly made how you like it. I highly recommend this tea joint than any others.  I used to go to other tea shoppes before but none matches the creativity of this place.

Update: the owner has a "secret menu" haha...if I knew what they are. Well, the matcha milk tea is very refreshing on a hot summer's day.

Update no. 2: the owner came up with new drink specialties. Fruit teas infused by lychee jelly bits, peach oolong tea. Recently her snack menu has undergone changes. Passion T now selling Asian Fusion snacks! Whenever you see Moo on the menu (for instance mac and moo) it is filet mignon meat stir fried in vegetables and  macaroni noodles! I tried the moo egg rolls, AWESOME! The owner came up with what I think to be superb fish sauce chicken wings! Don't be fooled, it is fried chicken wings and it does not come with sauce. You have to request and I suggest sriracha! 5 stars on the Asian Fusion.  They're open for Christmas and I know where I'll be. I guess traditional Christmas food will have competition? Lol!üòÄ

Anyway, Passion T does not disappoint. Enjoy the nice, easygoing atmosphere or ambiance.

Updated:  Sometime in April 2020, in the beginning of the pandemic, the store changed management. Sure the menu is still there, with additional menu items that the new owner added. Though i've only been there four times ever since, it wouldn't be fair for me to say if things had gotten better. Or not.<//review>

<text>Came here with a friend to try the place out. My go to drink is the wintermelon black tea drink with boba ($3.85) because not all places carry it.  We also got the popcorn chicken and chicken gizzard. I've been told that the San Jose area has excellent tea drinks and the caveat is,  I'll be comparing it to my go to place in NYC.

Wintermelon black tea with boba ($3.85) - the wintermelon flavor was okay, I thought a little muted. Similar with the tea. Not as strong as I thought it would be. I don't know in detail how their teas are made or what type of tea leaves they use or how long they brew it for but either my taste buds are dying or it's a little tamed. I guess one good thing is that it wasn't overly sweet.

Overall, their boba is spot on. It's soft, chewy, not hard, and it hasn't been sitting around for awhile. I thought the boba was still slightly warm after immediately trying upon receiving the drink. If I only had the boba itself, it would have been a 4* review. I know of other places where they do more stuff to the boba to more or less enhance or compliment the teas. Of course that's extra ingredients/overhead but that's part of business decision/planning. If all other stores are not as good as this store, no need to change your model. But there is room for improvement.

As for the foods, I thought they were fine. I don't think you come to an establishment like this for their food. It's rare for these places to serve food that is better than their drinks. Since their main focus are drinks and desserts, there is a lesser weighting factor from the foods. One unique thing about this place is chicken gizzard. You definitely don't see that often and it's very catered to a certain type of population. I think it makes them a little unique.

For now, I'm going to keep my options open and will definitely come back here to try their Earl Gray. I think that's another tea drink that takes a little care and finesse to get it right.</text><Response>None<//Response><UserId.>109028906014708659267<//UserId.>< Pics>

<Text>My day started in North Hollywood, California at the Big lots. We were looking for a patio set. They were out. They told us that the Canoga Park, California store had them. We drove to Canoga Park and guess what? They didn't have them. We spoke to this employee in Canoga Park that made it his mission to find it for us. He finally found a store in Santa Paula, California that had what we were looking for. He spoke to an employee named Jose. Jose asked his manager Chris if they can hold the items for us. The policy of the company is not to hold anything for customers, however given the circumstance, he made a decision to hold the two patio sets that we wanted. We drove all the way to Santa Paula and found both Jose and Chris. They were extremely friendly, kind and apologetic for all that we had gone through. Chris, the manager rang up the order for us. He then instructed Jose to take the items out to our truck. They both assisted in putting four large sized boxes on the truck. Chris was gracious enough to tie all of the boxes together so the boxes wouldn't shift or fall during transport. I tried to tip him and he refused to take it saying it was his pleasure to help. Overall the customer service at the Santa Paula, Ca store was excellent. 5.0 star rating

5/12/2017

I have been going to La Mode Salon for over four years now and I love this salon. The staff is amazing! I was greeted by Jessica and was asked if I needed anything then proceeded to inform my stylist Stephanie that I was here. It is refreshing to be greeted immediately with a smiling face and made to feel that you are a top priority.

The salon is amazing. Very clean, open and beautifully decorated. My favorite is the chandelier that brings a touch of elegance. The staff and other stylists are so friendly, warm and inviting.

My stylist is Stephanie Guest! I have been going to Stephanie for over four years! She is amazing! I always seem to want to make a color change to go darker. Stephanie listens intently and always has done what I have requested and also provided me with future options for color and highlights that would enhance the look and am trying to achieve. I have 100% confidence in Stephanie! She is a stylist that keeps up on the latest trends, knows what she is doing and understands the look that I am trying to achieve.

In addition, I very much value the fact that La Mode has stayed in business and Stephanie has remained there. So many times, salons close due to lack of business, poor client service...this is very important to me. I like to know that I have a solid salon to go to and a stylist that does not constantly change locations...I feel part of the La Mode Family...keep up the outstanding service you provide!!!

The salon is amazing. Very clean, open and beautifully decorated. My favorite is the chandelier that brings a touch of elegance. The staff and other stylists are so friendly, warm and inviting.

My stylist is Stephanie Guest! I have been going to Stephanie for over four years! She is amazing! I always seem to want to make a color change to go darker. Stephanie listens intently and always has done what I have requested and also provided me with future options for color and highlights that would enhance the look and am trying to achieve. I have 100% confidence in Stephanie! She is a stylist that keeps up on the latest trends, knows what she is doing and understands the look that I am trying to achieve.

In addition, I very much value the fact that La Mode has stayed in business and Stephanie has remained there. So many times, salons close due to lack of business, poor client service...this is very important to me. I like to know that I have a solid salon to go to and a stylist that does not constantly change locations...I feel part of the La Mode Family...keep up the outstanding service you provide!!!

< Review>
Arrived at almost 3PM on a Saturday to a full house. Grab a seat at the bar and was told we can still order brunch item. Also caught the last couple days of Oakland Restaurant Week. The brunch menu for Restaurant Week is a solid deal, 1 donut + coffee or tea (jade green was some really good green tea!), 1 cocktail, and 1 main entree (came in huge portion).
We tried the fried chicken with biscuit and pork sausage gravy (awesome fried chicken, crispy, juicy and flavorful) the kimchi fried rice with shoyu egg (4 halves üòÆ)

Tip:
1) Get the fried chicken and try with the orange hot sauce
2) Happy hour daily from 3-5PM (see picture for menu)<//Review>

<Time>1549039197307<//Time>< Review>
I came here for my 30th birthday during Restaurant Week and the team at Hopscotch was very accommodating leading up to dinner - very responsive over email, answering questions, giving me an option to add a customizable message on the menu, etc.

I didn‚Äôt have a cocktail but my friends did and they all enjoyed them. The Norte√±o comes to mind as a particularly good one with green pepper vodka (perhaps from St. George‚Äôs?). Nice selection of wine that is reasonably priced. As for the food, Restaurant Week for our group size was a set menu, family style.

A few key items: started off with a kale salad (üëçüèΩ), Kakiage - tempura veggie/bamboo shoots which was great, and burrata with squash (best of the bunch).

For the mains, the spatzel with brats was fine but nothing unique about it. Same with the buttermilk fried chicken which seems to be their most popular dish (not as much flavor as expected and ours were a bit dried out). The soba malfadine carbonara was great! I added some salt to bring out the flavors after breaking the yolk but I liked the fusion between Japanese + Italian.

Dessert was awesome. Loved the donut and mud pie combo. Donut could‚Äôve been hotter but I imagine it‚Äôs because of our large party + the extra 45 seconds of the HBD song üòÜ

Overall, I didn‚Äôt think it was worth the $40 price tag, mostly because the quantities weren‚Äôt on par. Now, this might be due to the group/family style/restaurant week factor but none of us left full. One note about their service: they graciously comped one meal as my gluten-free guest was mostly neglected throughout the meal. I had to ask several times what she could eat and what she couldn‚Äôt eat despite stating in advance and getting confirmation days before) her dietary restrictions. That bit was disappointing but this stuff happens and I appreciated their manager apologizing profusely and making amends. Would I return? Possibly but perhaps with a smaller group.<//Review>

< text>
We had a 10:30 am brunch reservation were the first guests to arrive.  The hostess asked us to wait and than asked if we had reservation I said yes and provided the name of reservation.
She proceeded to walk us out the door of the main dining to the overflow annex a cold less comfortable environment.  I thought it was extremely odd, trying not to assume the worst.
My party was disappointed started looking for new restaurant for brunch. The waitress was kind & closed the door the temperature of the room became acceptable and we stayed.

The food arrived  some was excellent and other items not so much the chicken appeared to be pre fried and fried again.

There was a lack of coffee choices no alternative milk.

They began seating people in our area 35 minutes later overheard party stating they did not have reservations.

I would not recommend this restaurant<//text>

< text>
Hopscotch is a tastefully laid out American Japanese fusion food affaire. Small restaurant with seating for maybe 30 inside, a few tables outside.

Our food was pretty stellar. Fried chicken, biscuits and gravy, country potatoes, all great. Drinks were good as well (gin fizz). We did have to wait over 30 minutes for our order to be retaken because our bartender forgot to put it in, so I have to detract a star for that; realistically, I don't see service being an issue at all normally.

Also a great selection of unique scotches which I can't wait to try next time. Be aware the prices are not cheap but the food portions are pretty generous. This place is worth a try, you won't regret it.< /text>

< text>
Excellent food and service. This is a bit of a hole-in-the-wall with four tables outside and maybe ten inside. You can also eat at the bar. Their mixed drinks are excellent and unusual. Our shared starter of tempura-fried vegetables was very tasty, but a bit on the greasy side. Two of us had the buttermilk fried chicken and one the halibut. All the mains were great. We shared one dessert, the doughnuts. Don't be put off by the name. Try it. Overall I would give Hopscotch five stars except I think it is overpriced. Three of us with drinks, a bottle of wine, one starter, one dessert and three mains racked up a bill of $270 with tip. That is very expensive for what and where it is.<//text>

<Rate>5< /Rate>< review>
I love this kind of upscale Japanese-American fusion food. I haven't seen that much Japanese-American fusion, so I thought that this place was pretty cool and unique. I really enjoyed the food here and the interesting flavors that come from combining Japanese cuisine with American cuisine. I came here for the brunch and got the Braised Pork Belly Benedict. It was very nontraditional and different from a regular eggs benedict. The pork belly had a soy sauce asian flavor which was very interesting in combination with the hollandaise. It was also very tender and fatty which added more richness to the dish. The dish as a whole was almost too rich and I'm glad it came with a side salad.<//review>

<UserId.>104142636624753609155<//UserId.><name>Dickie Henshall<//name><rate>5< /rate><Resp>None<//Resp>< Review>
We ordered the uni ravioli, the asparagus, and the fried chicken. The uni ravioli is a magic trick invented to allow you to imagine a sashimi scallop wrapped around uni is a ravioli, supported by shoshito oil and herbs. OMG. The asparagus, perfectly firm without any woodiness, had a lovely mayo sauce, flakes of parmesan, and the platonic ideal of anchovy slivers (silver skin, a gentle salty smoky flavor). The buttermilk fried chicken was slightly hot, and a confusing anatomy of white meat (even on the drumstick) and wonderfully crunchy crust. A house-made chili sauce, thin, clear, hot and still with flavor, was provide in a cruet. You must get yourself here.< /Review>

< Review>
This restaurants flavor profile and food combinations are terrible! That cannot be a true chef creating that menu. Cod is a soft fish great for stews or battering. They served it with cooked spinach and miso. It was an extremely mushy dish. No texture. The fried chicken came in a bed of cabbage. It was fried hard and had thin and dry batter. The sunchokes were tasty, but needed an aioli or some type of Sauce. The chicken could use some dipping sauce also. They served cold mozzarella on top of cooked veggies. And gave us tiny, cold, uncooked tofu cubes with what tasted like the sweet red sauce you get from the Chinese restaurant. Absolutely nothing about anything on that menu was worth our $150 meal. Fortunately the company paid for it, but we could've went ANYWHERE cheaper and had quality options. The idea is high end, but the food is not.< /Review>

<pics>None< /pics>< review>
A charming quaint local Oakland spot with wonderful food.  We sat at the bar and ordered what the bartender recommended which included beer steamed clams, kanpachi sashimi, and the duck liver pate and opted for the fried chicken for dinner.  All were quite good and wonderfully prepared.  The service was attentive and good.  The decor is that of a friendly neighborhood bistro.  I called a half an hour before we arrived asking if there was availability at the bar.  We had to wait about five minutes when we got there but then a spot cleared up for us.  It's nice that they have a few chairs outside and it's a pleasant place to wait and take in the city on a warm night.

We will definitely be back.< /review>

< date>
1417714536157</date>
<Review>Hopscotch can be a very conflicting experience.  Brunch is great; dinner is lackluster.  Service is great; then it sucks.  One dish can be amazing; the next dish can be a dud.  I've been here a few times, and always leave scratching my head, wondering how I should feel.  Here are some takeaways:

First of all, the place is TINY.  I think maybe eight tables and a bar with eight stools.  It can be very crowded, so factor that into your plans.

Brunch is very solid.  The fried chicken is out of this world, maybe the best I've had in California.  The Bloody Mary is fantastic.  They'll even do a solid French 75, which isn't always the best experience if the bartender doesn't know their stuff.  If you sit at the bar, the bartenders are always pleasant and your service (and your cocktails) will be great.  Get the donuts, you won't regret it.

A few days ago we went in for a Christmas special "whole lamb platter," which consisted of a few different cuts of lamb, broccoli romanesco, cauliflower puree, and cornbread.  It sounded good in the e-mail, but the dinner was just... underwhelming.  For $65 we got a "portion for two" that was generously made for one, and immediately regretted not ordering something else.  All of the food was fine, but none of it was special.

The service was also pretty bad.  When we asked for cocktail pairings instead of wine pairings, the waitress basically said, "Um, well, the wine is really good. Are you sure you don't want wine?" and then offered no help when it came to cocktails.  In a place that actually has a great bar, you'd think they would be more willing to talk cocktails.  We felt like we were being pushed hard towards the wine pairings in a gross, upselly-type way, and it was a bummer.

I keep thinking I should go back to Hopscotch and give them another try, because for every negative point, there's a positive point.  Really and truly, I've had some great bites and drinks here.  But it's just not solid enough to stay in my thoughts or stomach for long, especially with so many great restaurants in the Oakland/Berkeley area.

Hopscotch needs to up its game.  There are some ballers around here.</Review></record></dataset><record>

< Text>
My partner and I started with the Yonsei Oyster and the fries. The oyster came with uni, salmon roe, and citrus soy. I didn‚Äôt taste a citrus element, the soy was light like a dashi, but it was surprisingly really good in a decadent way and it felt refreshing in the Oakland heat. If I had known how delicious they were, I would have ordered a dozen of these!

The fries were crispy and it came with a Frenso chili aioli that was creamy, a touch spicy, and it‚Äôs something every fatty like me would enjoy.

I ordered the First Base Burger and it came with a house ground chuck, griddled beef tongue, pickled onions, and sesame aioli with a side of Kennebec chips. You can also add bacon or cheddar and I opted for the latter. It‚Äôs not a homerun, but still exciting in its own way. I asked for medium rare and received a rare patty but I found it to tender and juicy. The aioli was sparse so I can‚Äôt tell you what it tasted like, but the pickled onion added a nice contrast to the beef and the sweet bun.

My partner ordered the chicken club and it came with lettuce, cabbage, bacon, tomato, and fried chicken. It was simple but the fried chicken took it up a notch. I only had a bite but have to get it the next time we visit.

Items do not appear as described but we had a good meal here.<//Text>

<user>110288469148184652948<//user><Name>Denise Dang</Name>< date>
1419202286887</date>
<rate>4</rate>< Review>
Came here with a friend for brunch on a Sunday morning around 10:45. Since it was still early, we were seated right away, outside on the patio per our request. Service was wonderful and quick, and they made some nice suggestions for brunch, although their menu is really limited and very much Asian-inspired.

We started our meal with a carafe of Mimosas for $15, which equates to about 1.5 drinks per person. My friend had the kimchi fried rice with miso marinated jidori eggs. We hadn't expected her rice to be so moist and wet, more on the side of risotto than fried rice, though still good. I had the pork belly eggs benedict, which came with a side salad and skillet potatoes. The Benedict was good, though really rich with the creaminess of the egg yolk, hollandaise sauce, and pork belly fat. The side frisee salad had a nice tart vinegrette. The skillet potatoes came out pipping hot on a small cast iron skillet, though it was rather creamy and cheesy, more like potatoes au gratin than the skillet homefries I was expecting for brunch. Since the pork belly eggs benedict was already so rich, the potatoes seemed like excess. I wish I had gotten fruit as a side instead to even the meal out!

Street parking was easy to find. We found out afterwards that their is also a second half to the restaurant two doors down, so there's definitely more seating than the main location shows.<//Review>
